Default location of Perl executable is <code>/usr/bin/perl</code>. In case Perl is installed in a different location, the first line of all Perl scripts in the <code><b>twiki/bin</b></code> directory must be changed (alternatively you can create a symbolic link from <code><b>/usr/bin/perl</b></code> ). </li> </ul></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.26">r1.26</a> - 01&nbsp;Sep&nbsp;2001 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/MikeMannix">MikeMannix</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> Below installation steps assume that you have control over the web server configuraton files. In case you don't - you may be installing on an ISP-hosted server - follow the steps but use these directories instead: </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Added: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td><p /> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <h3><a name="Standard_Installation_Steps"> Standard Installation Steps </a></h3> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <h3><a name="Standard_Installation"> Standard Installation </a></h3> <p /> Request and download the TWiki %VERSION% distribution in Unix ZIP format from <a href="http://TWiki.org/download.html" target="_top">http://TWiki.org/download.html</a>. <p /> <h4><a name="Step_1_Create_Configure_the_Dire"> Step 1: Create &amp; Configure the Directories </a></h4> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FFD7D7" colspan ="2"><b> Deleted: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Request the TWiki distribution (in Unix ZIP format) from <a href="http://TWiki.org/download.html" target="_top">http://TWiki.org/download.html</a> . </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Here are example <code>httpd.conf</code> entries: </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <p /> <blockquote style="background-color:#f0f0f0"> <strong>Example <code>httpd.conf</code> entries:</strong> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Added: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td><p /> </blockquote> <p /> <h4><a name="Step_2_Check_the_Server_Director"> Step 2: Check the Server Directory Settings </a></h4> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> <ul> <li> Execute the <code>testenv</code> script from your browser ( <code>http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin/testenv</code> ). It shows a table with all CGI environment variables and tests the settings in your <code>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</code> configuration file. </li> </ul> </li> <li> Make sure PERL 5 and the PERL CGI library is installed on your system. Default location of PERL executable is <code>/usr/bin/perl</code> . In case PERL is installed in a different location, the first line of all perl scripts in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory need to be changed (alternatively you can create a symbolic link from <code>/usr/bin/perl</code> ). </li> <li> To be able to edit the perl scripts and .tmpl files it is necessary to <code>chown</code> and <code>chgrp -R twiki</code> so all the files have the owner you want. </li> <li> The scripts execute as <code>nobody</code> . Set the file permission of all Perl scripts in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory as executable to <code>-rwxr-xr-x</code> . </li> <li> Set the permission of all files below <code>twiki/data</code> so that they are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to 666 ( <code>-rw-rw-rw-</code> ). </li> <li> Set the permission of the <code>twiki/data</code> directory and all its subdirectories so that files in there are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to 777 ( <code>drwxrwxrwx</code> ). </li> <li> Set the permission of the <code>twiki/pub</code> directory and all its subdirectories so that files in there are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to 777 ( <code>drwxrwxrwx</code> ). </li> <li> Edit the file <code>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</code> and set the variables at the beginning of the file to your needs. </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> <ul> <li> Execute the <code>testenv</code> script from your browser ( <code>http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin/testenv</code> ). It shows a table with all CGI environment variables and tests the settings in your <code><b>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</b></code> configuration file. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> <p /> <h4><a name="Step_3_Enable_Perl_File_Permissi"> Step 3: Enable Perl File Permissions </a></h4> <p /> <ul> <li> Make sure Perl 5 and the Perl CGI library is installed on your system. Default location of Perl executable is <code>/usr/bin/perl</code> . In case Perl is installed in a different location, the first line of all perl scripts in the <code><b>twiki/bin</b></code> directory need to be changed (alternatively you can create a symbolic link from <code><b>/usr/bin/perl</b></code> ). <ul> <li> <strong>IMPORTANT:</strong> On most ISP virtual domain accounts, Perl CGI scripts require a <code><b>.cgi</b></code> extension to run. Some systems need <code><b>.pl</b></code>, the regular Perl extension. Change all <code><b>twiki/bin</b></code> scripts appropriately if necssary. </li> </ul> </li> <li> To be able to edit the Perl scripts and <code><b>.tmpl</b></code> files it is necessary to <code><b>chown</b></code> and <code><b>chgrp -R twiki</b></code> so all the files have the owner you want. </li> <li> The scripts execute as <code><b>nobody</b></code>. Set the file permission of all Perl scripts in the <code><b>twiki/bin</b></code> directory as executable to <code><b>-rwxr-xr-x</b></code> (755). </li> <li> Set the permission of all files below <code>twiki/data</code> so that they are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to <code><b>chmod</b></code> them to <code><b>-rw-rw-rw-</b></code> (666). </li> <li> Set the permission of the <code><b>twiki/data</b></code> directory and its subdirectories so that files in there are writable by user <code><b>nobody</b></code>. A simple way is to chmod them to <code><b>drwxrwxrwx</b></code> (777). </li> <li> Set the permission of the <code>twiki/pub</code> directory and all its subdirectories so that files in there are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to <code><b>drwxrwxrwx</b></code> (777). </li> </ul> <p /> <h4><a name="Step_4_Set_the_Main_Configuratio"> Step 4: Set the Main Configuration File </a></h4> <p /> <ul> <li> Edit the file <code><b>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</b></code> and set the variables at the beginning of the file to your needs. <ul> <li> Set the file extension in the <code>$scriptSuffix</code> variable to <code><b>cgi</b></code> or <code><b>pl</b></code> if required. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FFD7D7" colspan ="2"><b> Deleted: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Point your browser at <a href="http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin/view" target="_top">http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin/view</a> and start TWiki-ing away! </li> <li> Using your browser, edit the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiPreferences">TWikiPreferences</a> topic in the TWiki.TWiki web to set the WIKIWEBMASTER email address, the WEBCOPYRIGHT message and other preferences. </li> <li> Note in case the cgi scripts must have a file extension like <code>.pl</code> or <code>.cgi</code>: <ul> <li> Add the extension to all the scripts (except for the <code>.pm</code> ones) in <code>twiki/bin</code> </li> <li> Edit <code>wikicfg.pm</code> and set the file extension in the <code>$scriptSuffix</code> variable. </li> <li> If you use <code>.htaccess</code>, edit the file and add the file extension to <code>edit</code>, <code>view</code>, <code>preview</code>, etc. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Security issue: Directories <code>twiki/data</code> , <code>twiki/templates</code> and all its subdirectories should be set so that they are <strong>not</strong> visible as a URL. (Alternatively, move the directries to a place where they are not visible, and change the variables in <code>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</code> accordingly) </li> <li> Enable email notification of topic changes, <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiDocumentation#TWiki_Notification_of_Changes">Notification of Changes</a> has more. Using your browser, edit also the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebNotify">WebNotify</a> topic in all webs and set the users you want to notify. </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> <strong>Security issue:</strong> Directories <code>twiki/data</code> , <code>twiki/templates</code> and all its subdirectories should be set so that they are <strong>not</strong> visible as a URL. (Alternatively, move the directries to a place where they are not visible, and change the variables in <code>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</code> accordingly) </li> <li> Enable email notification of topic changes, <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiDocumentation#TWiki_Notification_of_Changes">Notification of Changes</a> has more. </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <h3><a name="Adding_Variables_Rendering_Rules"> Adding Variables &amp; Rendering Rules </a></h3> <p /> <ul> <li> Optional: You can add new rendering rules or new %VARIABLES%. To insure an easy upgrade of TWiki it is recommended to do this customization in <code>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</code> , not <code>twiki/bin/wiki.pm</code> . </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <h4><a name="Step_5_Finish_Up_from_Your_Brows"> Step 5: Finish Up from Your Browser </a></h4> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <h3><a name="Enabling_Basic_Authentication_ht"> Enabling Basic Authentication (.htaccess) </a></h3> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> Point your Web browser at <code><b>http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin/view</b></code> and start TWiki-ing away! </li> <li> Edit the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiPreferences">TWikiPreferences</a> topic in the <a href="http://twiki.org/cgi-bin/view/TWiki" title="'TWiki' on TWiki site, we know it!">TWiki:TWiki</a> web to set the WIKIWEBMASTER email address, the WEBCOPYRIGHT message and other preferences. </li> <li> If you use <code>.htaccess</code>, edit the file and add the file extension to <code>edit</code>, <code>view</code>, <code>preview</code>, etc. </li> <li> Edit the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebNotify">WebNotify</a> topic in all webs and set the users you want to notify. </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Optional: If you are on a non authenticated server (i.e. not using SSL) and you would like to authenticate users: <ul> <li> Rename file <code>.htaccess.txt</code> in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory to <code>.htaccess</code> and change it to your needs. For details consult the HTTP server documentation (for Apache server: <a href="http://www.apache.org/docs/mod/directives.html">[1]</a>, <a href="http://www.mcs.kent.edu/system/web_help/htaccess/introduction.html">[2]</a>). In particular, the following <font color="red">red</font> part needs to be configured correctly: <br> <code>Redirect <font color="red">/urlpath/to/TWiki/index.html</font> http://<font color="red">your.domain.com/urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/</font>view</code> <br> <code>AuthUserFile <font color="red">/filepath/to/TWiki/data/</font>.htpasswd</code> <br> <code>ErrorDocument 401 <font color="red">/urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/</font>oops/TWiki/TWikiRegistration?template=oopsauth</code> <ul> <li> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> The browser should ask for login name and password when you click on the <u>Edit</u> link. In case <code>.htaccess</code> does not have the desired effect you need to enable it: Add "AllowOverride All" to the Directory section of <code>access.conf</code> for your <code>twiki/bin</code> directory. </li> </ul> </li> <li> Copy the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistrationPub">TWikiRegistrationPub</a> topic to <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration">TWikiRegistration</a>. Do that by either editing the topics in theTWiki web, or by renaming the <code>.txt</code> and <code>.txt,v</code> files in the <code>twiki/data/TWiki</code> directory. <ul> <li> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> You can customize the registration form if needed, like deleting or adding input tags. The <code>name=""</code> parameter of the input tags must start with: <code>"Twk0..."</code> (if this is an optional entry), or <code>"Twk1..."</code> (if this is a required entry). This will ensure that the fields are processed correctly. </li> </ul> </li> <li> A new line containing user name and encrypted password gets added to the <code>data/.htpasswd</code> file when a users registers. The file that comes with the TWiki installation contains a few user accounts of TWiki core team members (needed for testing). You can edit the file and delete those lines. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> That's it for the standard virgin installation of TWiki. Read on to learn how to customize TWiki. </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <h3><a name="Generating_Site_Usage_Statistics"> Generating Site Usage Statistics </a></h3> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <h3><a name="Extra_Server_Level_Options"> Extra Server-Level Options </a></h3> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Optional: You can automatically generate usage statistics for all webs. To enable this: <ul> <li> Make sure variable <code>$doLogTopicView, $doLogTopicSave and $doLogTopicUpload</code> in <code>wikicfg.pm</code> are set. This will generate log entries in file <code>twiki/data/log&lt;date&gt;.txt</code> . </li> <li> Topic <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebStatistics">WebStatistics</a> must be present in all webs where you want to have statistics. You can use the topic in the Main web as a template. </li> <li> Call the <code>twiki/bin/statistics</code> script from a cron job, once a day is recommended. This will update the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/WebStatistics">WebStatistics</a> topics in all webs. </li> <li> <strong><em>Attention:</em></strong> The script must run as the same user as the CGI scripts are running, which is user <code>nobody</code> on most systems. Example crontab entry: <br> <code>0 0 * * * (cd /path/to/TWiki/bin; ./statistics &gt;/dev/null 2&gt;&amp;1)</code> </li> <li> There is a workaround in case you can't run the script as user <code>nobody</code> : Run the utility <code>twiki/bin/geturl</code> in your cron job and specify the URL of the <code>twiki/bin/statistics</code> script as a parameter. Example: <br> <code>0 0 * * * (cd /path/to/TWiki/bin; ./geturl mydomain.com /urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/statistics &gt;/dev/null 2&gt;&amp;1)</code> </li> <li> The <code>twiki/bin/statistics</code> script can also be executed as a CGI script, just enter the URL in your browser. Examples: <ul> <li> Update current month for all webs: <br> <code>http://mydomain.com/twiki/bin/statistics</code> </li> <li> Update current month for Main web only: <br> <code>http://mydomain.com/twiki/bin/statistics/Main</code> </li> <li> Update January 2000 for Main web: <br> <code>http://mydomain.com/twiki/bin/statistics/Main?logdate=200001</code> </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> Complete a Standard Installation and your new TWiki site should be up and running. You can develop and manage most aspects of your site from the browser interface. Core set-up functions require direct access to the server file system, via Telnet or FTP. You can make server-level site changes during installation, or at any time afterwards. </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <h3><a name="Creating_a_New_Web"> Creating a New Web </a></h3> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <h4><a name="Creating_a_New_Web"> Creating a New Web </a></h4> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Added: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td><p /> <h4><a name="Adding_Variables_Rendering_Rules"> Adding Variables &amp; Rendering Rules </a></h4> <p /> <ul> <li> You can add new rendering rules or new %VARIABLES%. To insure an easy upgrade of TWiki it is recommended to do this customization in <code>twiki/bin/wikicfg.pm</code> , not <code>twiki/bin/wiki.pm</code> . </li> </ul> <p /> <h4><a name="Enabling_Basic_Authentication_ht"> Enabling Basic Authentication (.htaccess) </a></h4> <p /> <ul> <li> If you are on a non authenticated server (i.e. not using SSL) and you would like to authenticate users: <ul> <li> Rename file <code>.htaccess.txt</code> in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory to <code>.htaccess</code> and change it to your needs. For details consult the HTTP server documentation (for Apache server: <a href="http://www.apache.org/docs/mod/directives.html">[1]</a>, <a href="http://www.mcs.kent.edu/system/web_help/htaccess/introduction.html">[2]</a>). In particular, the following <font color="red">red</font> part needs to be configured correctly: <br> <code>Redirect <font color="red">/urlpath/to/TWiki/index.html</font> http://<font color="red">your.domain.com/urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/</font>view</code> <br> <code>AuthUserFile <font color="red">/filepath/to/TWiki/data/</font>.htpasswd</code> <br> <code>ErrorDocument 401 <font color="red">/urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/</font>oops/TWiki/TWikiRegistration?template=oopsauth</code> <ul> <li> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> The browser should ask for login name and password when you click on the <u>Edit</u> link. In case <code>.htaccess</code> does not have the desired effect you need to enable it: Add "AllowOverride All" to the Directory section of <code>access.conf</code> for your <code>twiki/bin</code> directory. </li> </ul> </li> <li> Copy the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistrationPub">TWikiRegistrationPub</a> topic to <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration">TWikiRegistration</a>. Do that by either editing the topics in theTWiki web, or by renaming the <code>.txt</code> and <code>.txt,v</code> files in the <code>twiki/data/TWiki</code> directory. <ul> <li> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> You can customize the registration form if needed, like deleting or adding input tags. The <code>name=""</code> parameter of the input tags must start with: <code>"Twk0..."</code> (if this is an optional entry), or <code>"Twk1..."</code> (if this is a required entry). This will ensure that the fields are processed correctly. </li> </ul> </li> <li> A new line containing user name and encrypted password gets added to the <code>data/.htpasswd</code> file when a users registers. The file that comes with the TWiki installation contains a few user accounts of TWiki core team members (needed for testing). You can edit the file and delete those lines. </li> </ul> </li> </ul></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.25">r1.25</a> - 01&nbsp;Sep&nbsp;2001 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/MikeMannix">MikeMannix</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" You can edit the file and delete those lines. </li> </ul> </li> </ul></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.20">r1.20</a> - 11&nbsp;Jul&nbsp;2001 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Added: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> <ul> <li> Rename file <code>.htaccess.txt</code> in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory to <code>.htaccess</code> and change it to your needs. For details consult the HTTP server documentation (for Apache server: <a href="http://www.apache.org/docs/mod/directives.html">[1]</a>, <a href="http://www.mcs.kent.edu/system/web_help/htaccess/introduction.html">[2]</a>). <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> In case <code>.htaccess</code> does not have any effect you need to enable it: Add "AllowOverride All" to the Directory section of <code>access.conf</code> for your <code>twiki/bin</code> directory. </li> <li> Copy the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistrationPub">TWikiRegistrationPub</a> topic to <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration">TWikiRegistration</a>. You can customize the topic if needed. <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> You can delete or add new input tags to the registration form. The <code>name=""</code> parameter of the input tags must start with: <code>"Twk0..."</code> (if this is an optional entry), or <code>"Twk1..."</code> (if this is a required entry). This will ensure that the fields are processed correctly. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> <ul> <li> Rename file <code>.htaccess.txt</code> in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory to <code>.htaccess</code> and change it to your needs. For details consult the HTTP server documentation (for Apache server: <a href="http://www.apache.org/docs/mod/directives.html">[1]</a>, <a href="http://www.mcs.kent.edu/system/web_help/htaccess/introduction.html">[2]</a>). In particular, the following <font color="red">red</font> part needs to be configured correctly: <br> <code>Redirect <font color="red">/urlpath/to/TWiki/index.html</font> http://<font color="red">your.domain.com/urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/</font>view</code> <br> <code>AuthUserFile <font color="red">/filepath/to/TWiki/data/</font>.htpasswd</code> <br> <code>ErrorDocument 401 <font color="red">/urlpath/to/TWiki/bin/</font>view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration</code> <ul> <li> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> The browser should ask for login name and password when you click on the <u>Edit</u> link. In case <code>.htaccess</code> does not have the desired effect you need to enable it: Add "AllowOverride All" to the Directory section of <code>access.conf</code> for your <code>twiki/bin</code> directory. </li> </ul> </li> <li> Copy the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistrationPub">TWikiRegistrationPub</a> topic to <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiRegistration">TWikiRegistration</a>. Do that by either editing the topics in theTWiki web, or by renaming the <code>.txt</code> and <code>.txt,v</code> files in the <code>twiki/data/TWiki</code> directory. <ul> <li> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> You can customize the registration form if needed, like deleting or adding input tags. The <code>name=""</code> parameter of the input tags must start with: <code>"Twk0..."</code> (if this is an optional entry), or <code>"Twk1..."</code> (if this is a required entry). This will ensure that the fields are processed correctly. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> </ul></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.19">r1.19</a> - 16&nbsp;Mar&nbsp;2001 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Added: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td><p /> <h2><a name="TWiki_Installation_Notes"> TWiki Installation Notes </a></h2> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> Installation steps: </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <h3><a name="Installation_steps"> Installation steps </a></h3> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Enable email notification of topic changes, <A href="TWikiDocumentation#notification">Notification of Changes</A> has more. Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.17">r1.17</a> - 30&nbsp;Dec&nbsp;2000 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> <ul> <li> Note that user home topics are only located in the TWiki.Main web, so don't try to move them or create them in other webs. From any web you can refer to users located in the TWiki.Main web like <code>Main.UserName</code> or <code>%MAINWEB%.UserName</code>. </li> </ul> </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> -- <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a> - 24 Nov 2000 <br> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> -- <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a> - 29 Dec 2000 <br></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.16">r1.16</a> - 11&nbsp;Dec&nbsp;2000 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Set the file permission of all files below <code>twiki/data</code> to 666 ( <code>-rw-rw-rw-</code> ). </li> <li> Set the file permission of the <code>twiki/data</code> directory and all its subdirectories to 777 ( <code>drwxrwxrwx</code> ). </li> <li> Set the file permission of the <code>twiki/pub</code> directory to 777 ( <code>drwxrwxrwx</code> ). </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> Set the permission of all files below <code>twiki/data</code> so that they are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to 666 ( <code>-rw-rw-rw-</code> ). </li> <li> Set the permission of the <code>twiki/data</code> directory and all its subdirectories so that files in there are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to 777 ( <code>drwxrwxrwx</code> ). </li> <li> Set the permission of the <code>twiki/pub</code> directory and all its subdirectories so that files in there are writable by user <code>nobody</code>. A simple way is to chmod them to 777 ( <code>drwxrwxrwx</code> ). </li> </ul></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.15">r1.15</a> - 29&nbsp;Nov&nbsp;2000 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Added: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Using your browser, edit the <a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiPreferences">TWikiPreferences</a> topic in the TWiki.TWiki web to set the WIKIWEBMASTER email address, the WEBCOPYRIGHT message and other preferences. </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Note in case the cgi scripts are <strong><em>not</em></strong> running as user <code>nobody</code>: The <code>*,v</code> RCS repository files delivered with the installation package are locked by user <code>nobody</code> . In case the user is different (e.g. <code>www-data</code> ), it is not possible to check in files, this has the effect that the topic version number does not increase when saving a topic. In this case you need to unlock all repository files and lock them as user <code>www-data</code> (check the rcs man pages), or simply delete all the repository files. A simple way to switch the locker of the RCS files is to use sed: <br> <code>for f in *,v; do sed 's/nobody/www-data/' $f &gt; x; mv x $f; done</code> </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> Note in case the cgi scripts are <strong><em>not</em></strong> running as user <code>nobody</code>: The <code>*,v</code> RCS repository files delivered with the installation package are locked by user <code>nobody</code> . In case the user is different (e.g. <code>www-data</code> ), it is not possible to check in files, this has the effect that the topic version number does not increase when saving a topic. In this case you need to unlock all repository files and lock them as user <code>www-data</code> (check the rcs man pages), or simply delete all the repository files. A simple way to switch the locker of the RCS files is to use sed: <br> <code>for f in *,v; do sed 's/nobody\:/www-data\:/' $f &gt; x; mv x $f; done</code> </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> <ul> <li> Enable email notification of topic changes, <A href="TWikiDocumentation#notification">Notification of Changes</A> has more. </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> Enable email notification of topic changes, <A href="TWikiDocumentation#notification">Notification of Changes</A> has more. In case the user is different (e.g. <code>www-data</code> ), it is not possible to check in files, this has the effect that the topic version number does not increase when saving a topic. In this case you need to unlock all repository files and lock them as user <code>www-data</code> (check the rcs man pages), or simply delete all the repository files. </li> </ul> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> <ul> <li> Note in case the cgi scripts are <strong><em>not</em></strong> running as user <code>nobody</code>: The <code>*,v</code> RCS repository files delivered with the installation package are locked by user <code>nobody</code> . In case the user is different (e.g. <code>www-data</code> ), it is not possible to check in files, this has the effect that the topic version number does not increase when saving a topic. In this case you need to unlock all repository files and lock them as user <code>www-data</code> (check the rcs man pages), or simply delete all the repository files. A simple way to switch the locker of the RCS files is to use sed: <br> <code>for f in *,v; do sed 's/nobody/www-data/' $f &gt; x; mv x $f; done</code> </li> </ul> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> -- <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a> - 20 Aug 2000 <br> </td></tr><tr><td bgcolor="#40FF40" valign="top" width="1%">&gt;<br />&gt;</td><td> <p /> -- <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a> - 23 Sep 2000 <br></td></tr> </table> <br clear="all" /><table width="100%" border="3" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"> <tr bgcolor="#FFE0B0"> <td width="99%"> &nbsp;<tt><b>&lt;&lt;O&gt;&gt;</b></tt>&nbsp; Difference Topic <b><a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide">TWikiInstallationGuide</a></b> (<a href="/twiki/bin/view/TWiki/TWikiInstallationGuide?rev=r1.7">r1.7</a> - 21&nbsp;Aug&nbsp;2000 - <a href="/twiki/bin/view/Main/PeterThoeny">PeterThoeny</a>) </td> </tr> </table> <table width="100%" cellspacing="0"> <tr><td> </td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#D0FFD0" colspan ="2"><b> Changed: </b></td></tr> <tr><td bgcolor="#FF4040" valign="top" width="1%">&lt;<br />&lt;</td><td><p /> These installation steps use the Apache web server on Linux as an example. TWiki should run on other web servers and Unix systems as well. <p /> <strong><em>Note:</em></strong> These installation notes assume user <code>nobody</code> for all files manupulated by the cgi scripts (executed by the web server), and user <code>twiki</code> for all other files. You need to replace user <code>nobody</code> with an other user in case the web server executes the script with a different user ( default for Debian is <code>www-data</code> ). Also, you can substitute user <code>twiki</code> with your own user name. <p /> <ul> <li> Request the TWiki distribution (in Unix ZIP format) from <a href="http://TWiki.SourceForge.net/download.html" target="_top">http://TWiki.SourceForge.net/download.html</a> . </li> <li> Create directory <code>/home/httpd/twiki</code> and unzip the TWiki distribution to this directory. </li> <li> The <code>twiki/bin</code> directory of TWiki must be set as a cgi-bin directory. Add <code>/home/httpd/twiki/bin</code> to <code>/etc/httpd/conf/access.conf</code> with only <code>ExecCGI</code> option. </li> <li> The <code>twiki/pub</code> directory of TWiki must be set so that it is visible as a URL. Add <code>/home/httpd/twiki/pub</code> to <code>/etc/httpd/conf/access.conf</code> with normal access options (copy from /home/httpd/html). </li> <li> Now add <code>Alias</code> for <code>/twiki/pub</code> and <code>ScriptAlias</code> for <code>/twiki/bin</code> to <code>/etc/httpd/conf/srm-conf</code> . </li> <li> Restart Apache by <code>/etc/rc.d/rc5.d/S85httpd restart</code> . </li> <li> Test if the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory is cgi-enabled: <ul> <li> Enter the URL of that directory into your browser ( <code>http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin</code> ). It is not set correctly as cgi-bin in case you get something like <code>"Index of /twiki/bin"</code> . It is OK if you get a message like <code>"Forbidden. You don't have permission to access /twiki/bin/ on this server."</code> </li> <li> Execute the <code>testenv</code> script from your browser ( <code>http://your.domain.com/twiki/bin/testenv</code> ). It should show a table of all CGI environment variables. </li> </ul> </li> <li> Make sure PERL and the PERL CGI library is installed on your system. Default location of PERL executable is <code>/usr/bin/perl</code> . In case PERL is installed in a different location, the first line of all perl scripts in the <code>twiki/bin</code> directory need to be changed (alternatively you can create a symbolic link from <code>/usr
Instances1
Solution

Do not trust client side input and enforce a tight check in the server side. Disable server side includes.
Reference

http://www.carleton.ca/~dmcfet/html/ssi.html

Medium (Medium)X-Frame-Options Header Not Set
Description

X-Frame-Options header is not included in the HTTP response to protect against 'ClickJacking' attacks.

MethodGET
ParameterX-Frame-Options
Instances4669
Solution

Most modern Web browsers support the X-Frame-Options HTTP header. Ensure it's set on all web pages returned by your site (if you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. ALLOW-FROM allows specific websites to frame the web page in supported web browsers).
Reference

http://blogs.msdn.com/b/ieinternals/archive/2010/03/30/combating-clickjacking-with-x-frame-options.aspx
CWE Id16
WASC Id15
Source ID3

Low (Medium)X-Content-Type-Options Header Missing
Description

The Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.

Instances4742
Solution

Ensure that the application/web server sets the Content-Type header appropriately, and that it sets the X-Content-Type-Options header to 'nosniff' for all web pages.

If possible, ensure that the end user uses a standards-compliant and modern web browser that does not perform MIME-sniffing at all, or that can be directed by the web application/web server to not perform MIME-sniffing.
Other information

This issue still applies to error type pages (401, 403, 500, etc) as those pages are often still affected by injection issues, in which case there is still concern for browsers sniffing pages away from their actual content type.

At "High" threshold this scanner will not alert on client or server error responses.

CWE Id16
WASC Id15
Source ID3
Low (Medium)Absence of Anti-CSRF Tokens
Description

No Anti-CSRF tokens were found in a HTML submission form.

A cross-site request forgery is an attack that involves forcing a victim to send an HTTP request to a target destination without their knowledge or intent in order to perform an action as the victim. The underlying cause is application functionality using predictable URL/form actions in a repeatable way. The nature of the attack is that CSRF exploits the trust that a web site has for a user. By contrast, cross-site scripting (XSS) exploits the trust that a user has for a web site. Like XSS, CSRF attacks are not necessarily cross-site, but they can be. Cross-site request forgery is also known as CSRF, XSRF, one-click attack, session riding, confused deputy, and sea surf.

CSRF attacks are effective in a number of situations, including:

* The victim has an active session on the target site.

* The victim is authenticated via HTTP auth on the target site.

* The victim is on the same local network as the target site.

CSRF has primarily been used to perform an action against a target site using the victim's privileges, but recent techniques have been discovered to disclose information by gaining access to the response. The risk of information disclosure is dramatically increased when the target site is vulnerable to XSS, because XSS can be used as a platform for CSRF, allowing the attack to operate within the bounds of the same-origin policy.

Instances6298
Solution

Phase: Architecture and Design

Use a vetted library or framework that does not allow this weakness to occur or provides constructs that make this weakness easier to avoid.

For example, use anti-CSRF packages such as the OWASP CSRFGuard.

Phase: Implementation

Ensure that your application is free of cross-site scripting issues, because most CSRF defenses can be bypassed using attacker-controlled script.

Phase: Architecture and Design

Generate a unique nonce for each form, place the nonce into the form, and verify the nonce upon receipt of the form. Be sure that the nonce is not predictable (CWE-330).

Note that this can be bypassed using XSS.

Identify especially dangerous operations. When the user performs a dangerous operation, send a separate confirmation request to ensure that the user intended to perform that operation.

Note that this can be bypassed using XSS.

Use the ESAPI Session Management control.

This control includes a component for CSRF.

Do not use the GET method for any request that triggers a state change.

Phase: Implementation

Check the HTTP Referer header to see if the request originated from an expected page. This could break legitimate functionality, because users or proxies may have disabled sending the Referer for privacy reasons.
Other information

No known Anti-CSRF token [anticsrf, CSRFToken, __RequestVerificationToken, csrfmiddlewaretoken, authenticity_token, OWASP_CSRFTOKEN, anoncsrf, csrf_token, _csrf, _csrfSecret] was found in the following HTML form: [Form 1: "topic" ].
Reference

http://projects.webappsec.org/Cross-Site-Request-Forgery

http://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/352.html

MethodGET
ParameterX-XSS-Protection
Instances4692
Solution

Ensure that the web browser's XSS filter is enabled, by setting the X-XSS-Protection HTTP response header to '1'.
Other information

The X-XSS-Protection HTTP response header allows the web server to enable or disable the web browser's XSS protection mechanism. The following values would attempt to enable it:

X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block

X-XSS-Protection: 1; report=http://www.example.com/xss

The following values would disable it:

X-XSS-Protection: 0

The X-XSS-Protection HTTP response header is currently supported on Internet Explorer, Chrome and Safari (WebKit).

Note that this alert is only raised if the response body could potentially contain an XSS payload (with a text-based content type, with a non-zero length).
Reference

https://www.owasp.org/index.php/XSS_(Cross_Site_Scripting)_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet

https://www.veracode.com/blog/2014/03/guidelines-for-setting-security-headers/

Low (Medium)Private IP Disclosure
Description

A private IP (such as 10.x.x.x, 172.x.x.x, 192.168.x.x) or an Amazon EC2 private hostname (for example, ip-10-0-56-78) has been found in the HTTP response body. This information might be helpful for further attacks targeting internal systems.

Solution
